<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Grand tourer</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">"Gran turismo" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Gran_Turismo_(disambiguation)" title="Gran Turismo (disambiguation)">Gran Turismo</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="2032" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg/220px-Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg/330px-Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg/440px-Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lancia_Aurelia_GT_B20.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1951 <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Aurelia" title="Lancia Aurelia">Lancia Aurelia B20 GT</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <b>grand tourer</b> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>gran turismo</i></span>) (<b>GT</b>) is a performance and <a href="/wiki/Luxury_vehicle" title="Luxury vehicle">luxury automobile</a> capable of high speed and long-distance driving. The most common format is a two-door <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">coupé</a> with either a two-seat or a <a href="/wiki/2%2B2_(car_body_style)" title="2+2 (car body style)">2+2</a> arrangement.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1235" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg/220px-1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg/330px-1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg/440px-1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1962_Ferrari_250_GTO_34_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1962 <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_250_GTO" title="Ferrari 250 GTO">Ferrari 250 GTO</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The term derives from the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> phrase <i>gran turismo</i>, a tribute to the tradition of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_tour" title="Grand tour">grand tour</a>, used to represent automobiles regarded as grand tourers, able to make long-distance, high-speed journeys in both comfort and style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The grand touring concept is <a href="/wiki/Eurocentrism" title="Eurocentrism">eurocentric</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> the definition implies material differences in performance at speed, comfort, and amenities between elite automobiles and those of ordinary motorists. In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">post-war</a> United States, the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">Interstate Highway System</a> and wide availability of powerful <a href="/wiki/Straight-six_engine" title="Straight-six engine">Straight-six</a> and <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V8 engines</a> rendered the original meaning obsolete. European GT's did find success penetrating the American <a href="/wiki/Personal_luxury_car" title="Personal luxury car">personal luxury car</a> market, notably the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_SL-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz SL-Class">Mercedes-Benz SL-Class</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg/220px-Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg/330px-Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg/440px-Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aston_Martin_DB5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1963 <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DB5" title="Aston Martin DB5">Aston Martin DB5</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_of_the_Gran_Turismo_automobile">Evolution of the <i>Gran Turismo</i> automobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Evolution of the Gran Turismo automobile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Grand touring car design evolved from <a href="/wiki/Vintage_car" title="Vintage car">vintage</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_automobile" title="History of the automobile">pre-World War II</a> fast <a href="/wiki/Touring_car" title="Touring car">touring cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Streamliner" title="Streamliner">streamlined</a> <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">closed</a> <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">sports cars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-:22-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Italy developed the first <i>gran turismo</i> cars. The small, light-weight and <a href="/wiki/Aerodynamics" title="Aerodynamics">aerodynamic</a> <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">coupé</a>, named the <i><a href="/wiki/Berlinetta" title="Berlinetta">Berlinetta</a>,</i> originated in the <a href="/wiki/1930s" title="1930s">1930s</a>. A contemporary French concept, known as <i>Grande Routière,</i> emphasized style, elegance, luxury and gentlemanly trans-continental touring, were often larger cars than the smaller Italian <i>Gran Tursimos.</i> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Italian designers saw that compared to a <a href="/wiki/MG_T-type" title="MG T-type">traditional open two-seat sports car</a>, the increase in weight and frontal area of an enclosed cabin for the driver and mechanic (or passenger) could be offset by the benefits of <a href="/wiki/Streamliner" title="Streamliner">streamlining</a> to reduce <a href="/wiki/Aerodynamic_drag" title="Aerodynamic drag">drag</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Independent <i>carrozzeria</i> (<a href="/wiki/Coachbuilder" title="Coachbuilder">coachbuilders</a>) provided light and <a href="/wiki/Weymann_Fabric_Bodies" title="Weymann Fabric Bodies">flexible fabric coachwork</a> for powerful short-wheelbase fast-touring <a href="/wiki/Chassis" title="Chassis">chassis</a> by manufacturers such as <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo" title="Alfa Romeo">Alfa Romeo</a>. Later, <a href="/wiki/Carrozzeria_Touring_Superleggera" title="Carrozzeria Touring Superleggera">Carrozzeria Touring of Milan</a> would pioneer sophisticated <i><a href="/wiki/Superleggera" title="Superleggera">Superleggera</a></i> (super light-weight) <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a> bodywork, allowing for even more <a href="/wiki/Aerodynamics" title="Aerodynamics">aerodynamic</a> forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The additional comfort of an enclosed cabin was beneficial for the <a href="/wiki/Mille_Miglia" title="Mille Miglia">Mille Miglia</a> (Thousand Miles) road-race held in Italy's often wintry north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1929_Alfa_Romeo_6C_1750_GT">1929 <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_6C" title="Alfa Romeo 6C">Alfa Romeo 6C 1750 GT</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1929 Alfa Romeo 6C 1750 GT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1056" data-file-width="1408" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG/220px-Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG/330px-Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG/440px-Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alfa-Romeo_6C-1750-GTC-Touring.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alfa Romeo 6C 1750 GTC Berlinetta Carrozzeria Touring Mille Miglia 1932</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first automobile to be named <i>Gran Turismo</i> was the 1929 <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_6C" title="Alfa Romeo 6C">Alfa Romeo's 6C 1750 GT</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Weymann_Fabric_Bodies" title="Weymann Fabric Bodies">fabric-bodied</a> <i>Berlinetta</i> model by Carrozzeria Touring being winner of the <i><a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">Vetture Chiuse</a></i> (closed car) category at the 1931 Mille Miglia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> An improved and <a href="/wiki/Supercharger" title="Supercharger">supercharged</a> version, the 6C 1750 GTC <i>Gran Turismo Compressore</i>, won the <i><a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">Vetture a Guida Interna</a></i> (internally driven car) category of the 1932 Mille Miglia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1935_Fiat_508_Balilla">1935 <a href="/wiki/Fiat_508" title="Fiat 508">Fiat 508 Balilla</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1935 Fiat 508 Balilla">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1056" data-file-width="1408" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG/220px-Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG/330px-Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG/440px-Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_508-S-Balilla_BerlMM.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fiat 508 Balilla S Berlinetta Mille Miglia 1935</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>SIATA was a Turin, Italy-based Fiat tuner, typical of a popular class of Italian artisan manufacturers of small gran turismo, sports and racing cars—usually Fiat based—that came to be known in the 1970s as <i>Etceterini</i>, such as <a href="/wiki/Nardi_(carmaker)" title="Nardi (carmaker)">Nardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abarth" title="Abarth">Abarth</a>, Ermini and, in 1946, Cisitalia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> From this design came the <a href="/wiki/Siata" title="Siata">SIATA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Automobiles" title="Fiat Automobiles">Fiat</a> aerodynamic <i>gran turismo</i>-style <i>Berlinetta Mille Miglias</i> of 1933 and 1935.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferrari">Ferrari</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ferrari">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_(14013102437).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1036" data-file-width="1500" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_%2814013102437%29.jpg/220px-Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_%2814013102437%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_%2814013102437%29.jpg/330px-Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_%2814013102437%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_%2814013102437%29.jpg/440px-Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_%2814013102437%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ermini_1100_Berlinetta_Motto_-_MM_2014_-_(14013102437).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Etceterini</i>: Ermini 1100 Berlinetta Motto</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Enzo_Ferrari" title="Enzo Ferrari">Enzo Ferrari</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Scuderia Ferrari</a> had been the racing division of <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo" title="Alfa Romeo">Alfa Romeo</a> from 1929 until 1938, parted ways from Alfa Romeo in 1939: Ferrari's first car (itself an <i>Etceterini)</i> the Fiat-based <a href="/wiki/Auto_Avio_Costruzioni_815" title="Auto Avio Costruzioni 815">Auto Avio Costruzioni 815</a> <a href="/wiki/Sports_car_racing" title="Sports car racing">racing sports car</a>, debuted at the 1940 Mille Miglia. Two were produced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The first <i>real</i> Ferrari, the V12 <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_125_S" title="Ferrari 125 S">125 S</a>, also a racing sports car, debuted in 1947 at the <a href="/wiki/Piacenza" title="Piacenza">Piacenza</a> racing circuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Again, only two were produced, but they rapidly evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_159_S" title="Ferrari 159 S">159</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_166_S" title="Ferrari 166 S">166</a> models, including the 1949 Ferarri 166 Inter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cisitalia_202_SC">Cisitalia 202 SC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cisitalia 202 SC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_(16987804980).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1185" data-file-width="1600" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_%2816987804980%29.jpg/220px-Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_%2816987804980%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_%2816987804980%29.jpg/330px-Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_%2816987804980%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_%2816987804980%29.jpg/440px-Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_%2816987804980%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cisitalia_202_-_Mille_Miglia_2014_(16987804980).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cisitalia Tipo 202 SC Coupé Carrozzeria Pininfarina 1947</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Cisitalia 202 SC gained considerable fame for the outstanding design of its <a href="/wiki/Pininfarina" title="Pininfarina">Pininfarina</a> <a href="/wiki/Coachbuilder" title="Coachbuilder">coachwork</a>, and is credited with greatly influencing the style of subsequent <i><a href="/wiki/Berlinetta" title="Berlinetta">berlinetta</a></i> or <a href="/wiki/Fastback" title="Fastback">fastback</a> gran turismo coupés.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Fiat_1100" title="Fiat 1100">Fiat</a> based 1100 cc <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four-cylinder" title="Four-cylinder">four-cylinder</a> Cisitaila was no match on the race track for Ferrari's hand-built 2000 cc <a href="/wiki/V12_engine" title="V12 engine">V12</a>, and Ferrari dominated the 1949 Coppa Inter-Europa taking the first three places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-:12-16">[16]</a></sup> An 1100 cc class was hurriedly created, but not in time to save Cisitalia's business fortunes—the company's owner <a href="/wiki/Piero_Dusio" title="Piero Dusio">Piero Dusio</a> had already decamped to Argentina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was initially hoped by Italian motor industry observers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-17">[17]</a></sup> that the small and struggling Italian sports and racing car manufacturer, <a href="/wiki/Cisitalia" title="Cisitalia">Cisitalia</a>, would find in the 1949 Coppa Inter-Europa regulations (initially called <i>Turismo Veloce</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> or Fast Touring) a category for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cisitalia_202" title="Cisitalia 202">Cisitalia Tipo 202 SC</a>—the road-going production <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">coupé</a> version of Cisitalia's single-seat <a href="/wiki/Cisitalia_Grand_Prix" title="Cisitalia Grand Prix">D46</a> racing car and two-seat 202 open sports car.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maserati_A6_1500">Maserati A6 1500</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Maserati A6 1500">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3103" data-file-width="4891" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg/220px-Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg/330px-Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg/440px-Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maserati_A6_1500_-_Museo_Enzo_Ferrari_-_fvr.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maserati A6 1500 Coupé Carrozzeria Pininfarina 1947</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Maserati_A6" title="Maserati A6">Maserati A6 1500</a> won the 1500 cc class at the 1949 Coppa-Europa. It was driven by<a href="/wiki/Franco_Bordoni" title="Franco Bordoni">Franco Bordoni</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Flying_ace" title="Flying ace">fighter ace</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Regia_Aeronautica" title="Regia Aeronautica">Regia Aeronautica</a> who had debuted as a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racing_driver" title="Racing driver">pilota da corsa</a></i> at the 1949 <a href="/wiki/Mille_Miglia" title="Mille Miglia">Mille Miglia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:12-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:112_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-:112-19">[19]</a></sup> The A6 1500 was the first road going production automobile to be offered by the <a href="/wiki/Maserati" title="Maserati">Maserati</a> factory, featuring a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tubular_chassis" title="Tubular chassis">tubular chassis</a> with <a href="/wiki/Independent_suspension" title="Independent suspension">independent front suspension</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coil_spring" title="Coil spring">coil springs</a>, the 1500 cc <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Six-cylinder_engine" title="Six-cylinder engine">six-cylinder</a> being derived from the Maserati brothers pre-war <i><a href="/wiki/Voiturette" title="Voiturette">voiturette</a></i> racing engines. The body of the A6 1500 was an elegant two-door fast-back coupe body, also by Pinin Farina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferrari_166_.27Inter.27">Ferrari 166 'Inter'</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ferrari 166 'Inter'">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1919" data-file-width="2552" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG/220px-1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG/330px-1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG/440px-1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1949_Ferrari_166_Inter_Coup%C3%A9_Touring_p2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferrari 166 Inter Coupé Carrozzeria Touring 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_166_Inter" title="Ferrari 166 Inter">Ferrari 166 'Inter'</a> S coupé model won the 1949 Coppa Inter-Europa. Regulations stipulated body form and dimensions but did not at this time specify a minimum production quantity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-:3-17">[17]</a></sup> The car was driven by Bruno Sterzi, and is recognized as the first Ferrari <i>gran turismo</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>After that race, governing body CSAI officially introduced a new class, called <i>Gran Turismo Internazionale</i>, for cars with production over thirty units per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> thereby ruling out Ferrari's hand-built <i>berlinettas</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1951_Ferrari_212_Export">1951 Ferrari 212 Export</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1951 Ferrari 212 Export">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1635" data-file-width="2794" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg/220px-Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg/330px-Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg/440px-Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari_212_Vignale_2_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferrari 212 Export Vignale Coupé 1951</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ferrari's response for the new <i>Gran Tursimo</i> championship was the road/race Ferrari 212. Twenty-seven short-wheelbase competition versions called Export, some with increasingly popular <i>gran turismo</i>-style <i>berlinetta</i> coupé coachwork, were produced for enthusiasts (Ferrari called the very first example 212 <i>MM</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>) while the road verson was called <i>Inter</i>. The Ferrari 212 Export featured long-range fuel tanks, high compression pistons and triple <a href="/wiki/Weber_carburetor" title="Weber carburetor">Weber 32 DCF carburettors</a>; power was 170 bhp from the 2600cc <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Colombo_engine" title="Ferrari Colombo engine">Gioacchino Colombo-designed 'short-block' V12 engine</a>, evolved from the earlier Ferrari 166 (2000cc) and 195 (2300cc).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> All versions came with the standard Ferrari five-speed non-synchromesh gearbox and hydraulic drum brakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> All 1951 Ferraris shared a double tube frame chassis design evolved from the 166. <a href="/wiki/Double_wishbone_suspension" title="Double wishbone suspension">Double-wishbone front suspension</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transverse_leaf_spring" title="Transverse leaf spring">transverse leaf spring</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Suspension_(vehicle)" title="Suspension (vehicle)">live rear axle</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-elliptic_leaf_spring" title="Semi-elliptic leaf spring">semi-elliptic leaf springs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radius_rod" title="Radius rod">radius rods</a> were employed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The Ferrari 212 Export (212 MM) <i>gran turismo berlinetta</i> (chassis no. 0070M) debuted in first-place overall at the April 1951 Coppa Inter-Europa, driven by Luigi Villoresi,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and in June (chassis no. 0092E) was first in the <i>Gran Turismo</i> category at the Coppa della Toscana driven by Milanese Ferrari concessionaire and proprietor of Scuderia Guastalla, Franco Cornacchia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The 212 Export continued to serve Ferrari well in the Sports and GT categories until replaced by the 225 S, and although it would later be overshadowed by the internationally famous 250 GT, the 212 Export was an important model in the successful line of Colombo-engined V12 GT cars that made Ferrari legendary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1951_Lancia_Aurelia_B20_GT">1951 Lancia Aurelia B20 GT</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1951 Lancia Aurelia B20 GT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_(5674066554).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_%285674066554%29.jpg/220px-Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_%285674066554%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_%285674066554%29.jpg/330px-Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_%285674066554%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_%285674066554%29.jpg/440px-Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_%285674066554%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5809_(5674066554).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lancia Aurelia B20 GT 1951</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Even more impressive than the new Ferrari in 1951 was the stunnng <i>Gran Turismo</i> racing debut of Lancia's <a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lancia_Aurelia_B20" title="it:Lancia Aurelia B20">Aurelia B20 GT.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lancia had begun production in 1950 of their technically advanced Aurelia sedan. At the 1951 Turin Motor Show, the <a href="/wiki/Pininfarina" title="Pininfarina">Pinin Farina</a>-bodied <i>Gran Tursimo</i> B20 Coupé version was unveiled to an enthusiastic motoring public. Here, finally, according to author Jonathan Wood,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-36">[36]</a></sup> was a fully realized production GT car, representing the starting point of the definitive Grand Tourer:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_(5673932402).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_%285673932402%29.jpg/220px-Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_%285673932402%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_%285673932402%29.jpg/330px-Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_%285673932402%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_%285673932402%29.jpg/440px-Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_%285673932402%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autoitalia_Brooklands_30th_April_2011_DSC_5681_(5673932402).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lancia Aurelia B20 GT 1951</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg/220px-Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg/330px-Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg/440px-Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lancia_aurelia_b20.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lancia Aurelia B20 GT 1951</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote>
<p>"This outwardly conventional saloon bristled with innovation and ingenuity, in which the masterly hand of <a href="/wiki/Vittorio_Jano" title="Vittorio Jano">Vittorio Jano</a> is apparent. In the B20 are elements of the Cistalia of 1947, coupés which Pinin undertook on a 6C Alfa Romeo and Maserati in 1948, along with the Fiat 1100 S coupé with its rear accommodation for children. The original Aurelia had been under-powered and, in 1951, the V6 was enlarged to 1991 cc, which was also extended to the coupé, though in 75 rather than 70 bhp form as the B20 was developed as a sporting model in its own right. In addition the B20 had a shorter wheelbase and a higher rear axle ratio, making it a 100 mph car. Lancia chose the <i>Gran Turismo</i> name for its new model and the suggestion could only have come from Vittorio Jano hinself, for had he not been responsible for the original 1750 Alfa Romeo of the same name back in 1929?" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Four <i>semi-ufficiali</i> works B20 GTs, together with a number of privateer entrants, were sent to the Mille Miglia in April, 1951, where the factory <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bracco" title="Giovanni Bracco">Bracco</a> / <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Maglioli" title="Umberto Maglioli">Maglioli</a> car finished second overall, behind only a Ferarri sports racer of twice the engine capacity. Lancia Aurelias swept the GT 2.0 Liter division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In June 1951, Bracco was partnered with the 'father of GT racing' himself, Johnny Lurani, to race a B20 GT at Le Mans, where they were victorious in the 2.0 Liter sportscar division, placing a very creditable 12th overall. A 1-2 finish at the famous Coppa d’Oro delle Dolomiti,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> among other victories including the 6 Ore di Pescara,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> rounded out an astonishing debut racing season for this ground-breaking automobile, winning its division in the Italian GT Championship for Umberto Castiglionoi in <a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Risultati_sportivi_della_Lancia_Aurelia" title="it:Risultati sportivi della Lancia Aurelia">1951</a>. Lancia B20 GTs would go on to win the Over 2.0 Liter Italian GT Championship in 1953, 1954 and 1955 with the <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Aurelia#Third_series" title="Lancia Aurelia">B20-2500</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1952_Fiat_8V_.22Otto_Vu.22">1952 Fiat 8V "Otto Vu"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title='Edit section: 1952 Fiat 8V "Otto Vu"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg/220px-Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg/330px-Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg/440px-Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_8V_Zagato_rear.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fiat 8V Zagato</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg/220px-Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg/330px-Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg/440px-Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_8V_Zagato.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fiat 8V Zagato</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A surprise to the international press,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:102_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-:102-40">[40]</a></sup> who were not expecting a <i>gran turismo berlinetta</i> from Italy's largest manufacturer of standard touring models, the <a href="/wiki/Fiat_8V" title="Fiat 8V">Fiat 8V "Otto Vu"</a> was unveiled at the Geneva Salon in March 1952 to international acclaim. Although not raced by the factory, the Otto Vu <i>was</i> raced by a number of private owners. Vincenzo Auricchio and Piero Bozzinio raced to fifth in the Gran Turismo category of the 1952 Mille Miglia, and Ovidio Capelli placed third in the GT 2000 cc class at the Giro della Toscana in June, with a special race-spec lightweight <a href="/wiki/Zagato" title="Zagato">Zagato</a> coupe; the GT category overall at this event was won by Franco Cornacchia's Ferrari 212 Export (refer above).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Capelli and the 8V Zagato topped this accomplishment by winning the GT category of the Pescara 12 Hours in August, ahead of two Lancias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The new Fiat 8V garnered sufficient competition points over the season to become the national two-liter GT Champion (a feat it repeated every year until 1959). <a href="/wiki/Elio_Zagato" title="Elio Zagato">Elio Zagato</a>, the coachbuilder's son, was successful in competition with the Otto Vu in 1954 and 1955,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> attracting further customer interest and leading Zagato to eventually develop two different GT racing versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:102_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-:102-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 8V Otto Vu earned its name courtesy of its high performance V8 engine (Ford having already trademarked "V8").</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1680" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg/220px-Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg/330px-Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg/440px-Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari_250_Europa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferrari 250 Europa</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1956_Ferrari_250_GT">1956 Ferrari 250 GT</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1956 Ferrari 250 GT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="943" data-file-width="1726" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg/220px-Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg/330px-Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg/440px-Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari-250-GT-Berlinetta-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferrari 250 GT</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2276" data-file-width="3034" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg/220px-Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg/330px-Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg/440px-Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferrari_250_GTO_at_concorso.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferrari 250 GTO</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote>
<p>"The 250GT Ferrari must surely represent the ultimate in modern high-speed sporting travel, or GT competition, and holds today a position similar to the Bugatti 57SC of 1939. In 1962 the GTO Ferrari <i>coupés</i> had a remarkable season of successes in G.T. racing and have become the standard by which any competition <i>coupé</i> is measured, and by steady development [the Ferrari 250GT] has become one of the world's greatest cars." MOTOR SPORT, March 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-:10-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>1953 saw the first serious attempt to series produce the Ferrari motor car, two models of the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_250" title="Ferrari 250">Type 250 Europa</a> being produced. The cars were an evolution of the previous models, available with either the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Colombo_engine" title="Ferrari Colombo engine">Colombo</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Lampredi_engine" title="Ferrari Lampredi engine">Lampredi</a> versions of the 250 V12 engine, coil spring front suspension, an improved sports gearbox (four speeds) with <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">synchromesh</a>, large <a href="/wiki/Drum_brake" title="Drum brake">drum brakes</a> and luxurious outfitting. A few appeared in motorsports but did not initially threaten the international <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_300_SL" title="Mercedes-Benz 300 SL">Mercedes-Benz 300 SL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porsche_356" title="Porsche 356">Porsche 356</a> competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-:10-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"In the Mille Miglia of 1956 the first of the lightweight Grand Touring <i>coupés,</i> driven by <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Gendebien" title="Olivier Gendebien">Gendebien</a>, battled with the Mercedes 300SL of <a href="/wiki/Paul_Alfons_von_Metternich-Winneburg" title="Paul Alfons von Metternich-Winneburg">Metternich</a> and Einsendel<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> to come in fifth overall and first in G.T. over 2,000 c.c. The G.T. Ferrari had arrived!" MOTOR SPORT, March 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-:10-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>After its 1956 debut, the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_250" title="Ferrari 250">250 GT</a> "went from strength to strength". Powered by the Colombo 250 engine, output was up to 240 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower" title="Horsepower">b.h.p</a>. at 7,000 r.p.m. A <a href="/wiki/Wheelbase" title="Wheelbase">short-wheelbase</a> (SWB) version of the 250 chassis was employed for improved <a href="/wiki/Automobile_handling" title="Automobile handling">handling and road-holding</a> in corners, and top speed was up to 157 <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/MPH" title="MPH">m.p.h.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-46">[46]</a></sup> In 1957 Gendebien finished third overall in the Mille Miglia, and won the "index of performance". <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_de_Portago" title="Alfonso de Portago">Alfonso de Portago</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> won the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France_Automobile" title="Tour de France Automobile">Tour de France</a> and GT races at <a href="/wiki/Montlh%C3%A9ry" title="Montlhéry">Montlhéry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipio_XIII" title="Municipio XIII">Castelfusano</a> in a lightweight <a href="/wiki/Carrozzeria_Scaglietti" title="Carrozzeria Scaglietti">Carrozzeria Scaglietti</a> 250 GT. Gendebien became a <i>gran turismo</i> specialist in 250 GTs when he wasn't driving sports racing <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_TR" title="Ferrari TR">Ferrari <i>Testa Rossas</i></a> ("Red Heads" for their red engine covers), achieving success in both the Giro Sicilia and Tour de France.</p>
<p>In 1958, sports racing <i>Testa Rossas</i> swept the <a href="/wiki/World_Sportscar_Championship" title="World Sportscar Championship">Manufacturer's Championship</a>, and in 1959 the T.R. engine was adapted to the 250 GT. The <a href="/wiki/Spark_plug" title="Spark plug">spark plugs</a> were relocated and each <a href="/wiki/Cylinder_(engine)" title="Cylinder (engine)">cylinder</a> now had a separate <a href="/wiki/Cylinder_head_porting" title="Cylinder head porting">intake port</a>. Larger <a href="/wiki/Weber_carburetor" title="Weber carburetor">Weber twin-choke carburetors</a> were employed in a triple configuration (sports racing T.R.s employed six) and some special customer cars had three four-choke Webers (one <a href="/wiki/Venturi_effect" title="Venturi effect">choke</a> per cylinder). <a href="/wiki/Dry_sump" title="Dry sump">Dry-sump lubrication</a> was employed, and the <a href="/wiki/Valve_timing" title="Valve timing">camshaft valve timing</a> was only slightly less than the full-race <i>Testa Rossas</i>. G.T. power was up to 267 b.h.p. at 7,000 r.p.m. (240 b.h.p at 6,800 rpm for road versions). Experiments were conducted with Dunlop disc brakes, which were adopted in 1960, along with an even shorter wheelbase for <i>competizione</i> versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1962, the definitive competition gran turismo was unveiled, the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_250_GTO" title="Ferrari 250 GTO">250 GTO</a>. A full <i>Testa Rossa</i> engine was employed (albeit with black crinkle-finish engine covers) with six twin-choke Webers. Power was up to 300 b.h.p. at 7,400 r.p.m. and with a lightweight 2000 lb body and chassis: the car was an immediate winner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Remarkable as it might be on the circuit, it is also a remarkable machine on the road. One American Ferrarist, who owned and raced many G.T. Ferraris, commented that the G.T.O. is an even more pleasant car on the road! He maintains that it is most tractable and overheating in traffic congestions is no problem. In its short lifetime the 250GTO has established an enviable record. It is also one of the most sought after competition cars as evidenced by recent European suggestions that "black market" G.T.O.s bring higher prices than new ones. The demand is greater than the supply." MOTOR SPORT, March 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In November 2016, it was reported that a 1962 Ferrari 250 GTO was being offered for public sale—normally brokers negotiate deals between extremely wealthy collectors "behind closed doors". GTOs had previoulsy been auctioned in 2014 and 1990. The 2017 sale was expected to reach USD $56,000,000.00, the particular GTO concerned (the second of just thirty-six ever made) thus set to become the world's most expensive car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_of_Racing">Impact of Racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Impact of Racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Italian <a href="/wiki/Mille_Miglia" title="Mille Miglia">Mille Miglia</a>, held from 1927 to 1957, was central to the evolution of the <i>gran turismo</i> concept. The event was one of the most important on the Italian motor-sport calendar, and could attract up to five million spectators. Winning drivers such as <a href="/wiki/Tazio_Nuvolari" title="Tazio Nuvolari">Tazio Nuvolari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Caracciola" title="Rudolf Caracciola">Rudolf Caracciola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Moss" title="Stirling Moss">Stirling Moss</a>; and manufacturers such as Alfa Romeo, <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, Ferrari and <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> would become household names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg/220px-Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg/330px-Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg/440px-Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alfa_Romeo_1938_2900_B_Speciale.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alfa Romeo 2900B Carrozzeria Touring Le Mans 1938</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to Enzo Ferrari:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"In my opinion, the Mille Miglia was an epoch-making event, which told a wonderful story. The Mille Miglia created our cars and the Italian automobile industry. The Mille Miglia permitted the birth of GT, or grand touring cars, which are now sold all over the world. The Mille Miglia proved that by racing over open roads for 1,000 miles, there were great technical lessons to be learned by the petrol and oil companies and by brake, clutch, transmission, electrical and lighting component manufacturers, fully justifying the old adage that motor racing improves the breed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Mille Miglia is still celebrated today as one of the world's premier historic racing events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>A closed sports coupé almost prevailed at <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">Le Mans</a> in 1938, when a Carrozziera Touring-bodied <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_8C" title="Alfa Romeo 8C">Alfa Romeo 8C 2900B</a>, driven by <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Sommer" title="Raymond Sommer">Raymond Sommer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clemente_Biondetti" title="Clemente Biondetti">Clemente Bionedetti</a>, led the famous 24-hour race from the third lap until early Sunday afternoon, retiring only due to engine problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CSAI">CSAI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: CSAI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="573" data-file-width="800" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg/220px-BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg/330px-BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg/440px-BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BMW_328_Mille_Miglia_Coupe_1940.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
BMW 328 Coupé Carrozzeria Touring Mille Miglia 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Italy's national governing body of motorsport was the <i>Commissione Sportiva Automobilistica Italiana</i> (CSAI). <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Lurani" title="Giovanni Lurani">Count Giovanni Lurani Cernuschi</a> (popularly known as Johnny Lurani was a key commissioner. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> He was also a senior member of the world governing body, the <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile">Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile</a></i> (FIA)). <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lurani was impressed by the dominant performance at the Mille Miglia in 1940, by a Carroziera Touring-bodied <a href="/wiki/BMW_328" title="BMW 328">BMW 328</a> coupé, winning the event at over 100 mph average speed, driven by <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Huschke_von_Hanstein" title="Fritz Huschke von Hanstein">Fritz Huschke von Hanstein</a> and <a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_B%C3%A4umer" title="de:Walter Bäumer">Walter Bäumer</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-:22-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"The BMW team included a splendid aerodynamic <i>Berlinetta</i>, wind tunnel designed by German specialists, that was extremely fast at 135 mph... I couldn't believe the speeds these BMWs were capable of."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-:22-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Lurani was instrumental in designing the regulations for the Italian 1937 <i>Turismo Nazionale</i> championship, whereby production vehicles approved by the CSAI were raced with the original chassis and engine layout as specified in the factory catalog and available for customers to buy; engines could be tuned and bored out, but the bodywork had to conform to regulations. The CSAI were concerned that FIA (known as AIACR at the time) 'Annexe C' Sports cars were becoming little more than thinly-disguised two-seat <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_motor_racing" title="Grand Prix motor racing">Grand Prix</a> racers, far removed from the cars ordinary motorists could purchase from the manufacturers' catalogs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The CSAI was shut down by the Italian <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascist</a> government under <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Mussolini</a> at the end of 1937, and replaced with a new organisation called FASI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Fascist_Party" title="National Fascist Party">Italian Fascists</a>, as in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, sought control of motor racing as an important vehicle for national prestige and <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> FASI replaced <i>Turismo Nazionale</i> with the less strictly regulated <i>Sports Nazionale</i> championship, which ran in 1938 and 1939. Postwar, the CSAI was re-established and in 1947 Italian national championships were held for both <i>Sports Internazionale</i> (FIA Annexe C sports cars) and <i>Sports Nazionale</i>. <i>Sports Nazionale</i> was abolished in 1948, creating the opportunity for a new category in 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1949_Coppa_Inter-Europa">1949 Coppa Inter-Europa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1949 Coppa Inter-Europa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Sports_car_racing" title="Sports car racing">race</a> specifically for grand touring motor cars was the 1949 Coppa Inter-Europa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-:8-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-:9-65">[65]</a></sup> held over three hours on 29 May, at the 6.3 kilometer <a href="/wiki/Autodromo_Nazionale_Monza" title="Autodromo Nazionale Monza">Autodromo Nazionale di Monza</a> (Italy).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-66">[66]</a></sup> It was won by a limited production Ferrari V12.</p>
<p>After this race, governing body CSAI officially introduced a new class, called <i>Gran Turismo Internazionale</i>, for 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-67">[67]</a></sup> The regulations were drawn up by Johhny Lurani and fellow Italian motor racing journalist and organizer Corrado Filippini,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> requiring for qualification the production of thirty models per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> thereby ruling out, for the time being, Ferrari's hand-built <i>berlinettas</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950_Mille_Miglia">1950 Mille Miglia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1950 Mille Miglia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_(14055528997).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1043" data-file-width="1500" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_%2814055528997%29.jpg/220px-Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_%2814055528997%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_%2814055528997%29.jpg/330px-Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_%2814055528997%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_%2814055528997%29.jpg/440px-Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_%2814055528997%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alfa_Romeo_6C_2500_SS_-_MM_2014_-_(14055528997).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alfa Romeo 6C 2500 SS</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_(10966804744).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_%2810966804744%29.jpg/220px-1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_%2810966804744%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_%2810966804744%29.jpg/330px-1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_%2810966804744%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_%2810966804744%29.jpg/440px-1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_%2810966804744%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1949_Fiat_1100_S_Mille_Miglia_(10966804744).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fiat 1100 S Coupé 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the third weekend of April 1950, it was the turn of the annual Mille Miglia, one-thousand miles from Brescia to Rome and back over closed public roads, to include a <i>Gran Turismo Internazionale</i> category for the first time. Twenty-four cars were entered in the <i>Gran Turismo</i> <i>Internazionale</i> category, including Alfa Romeo 6C 2500 SS Coupé Touring, Cisitalia 202B <i>berlinetta</i> and <a href="/wiki/Fiat_1100_(1937)" title="Fiat 1100 (1937)">Fiat 1100 S</a> coupé. The field was rounded out by a solitary Fiat-based SIATA Daina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Alfa Romeo took first place in the <i>Gran Turismo</i> <i>Internazionale</i> category (a creditable tenth overall) and also second place in category, followed by three Cisitalias. The overall race winning <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_195_S" title="Ferrari 195 S">Ferrari 195 S</a> was also a <i>berlinetta</i> coupe, but in the over 2000 Sports car class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Schwelm Cruz and Alfa Romeo repeated the success the 1950 Targa Florio and Mille Miglia by winning the <i>Gran Turismo</i> category at the Coppa della Toscana in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> An Alfa Romeo 6C 2500, driven by Salvatore Amendola, was also victorious in the <i>Gran Turismo</i> category of the <a href="/wiki/Coppa_d%27_Oro_delle_Dolomiti" title="Coppa d' Oro delle Dolomiti">Coppa d' Oro delle Dolomiti</a> in July, run through the <a href="/wiki/Dolomites" title="Dolomites">Dolomite Mountains</a>, starting and finishing in the town of <a href="/wiki/Cortina_d%27Ampezzo" title="Cortina d'Ampezzo">Cortina d'Ampezzo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> An Alfa Romeo 6C 2500 took the <i>Gran Turismo</i> honours again at the Giro delle Calabria in August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Like the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_400" title="Bristol 400">Bristol 400</a>, the Alfa Romeo 6C 2500 was based on a pre-war design, and is considered by some to be the last of the classic Alfa Romeos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950_Coppa_Inter-Europa">1950 Coppa Inter-Europa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1950 Coppa Inter-Europa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_(4637035235).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="1280" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_%284637035235%29.jpg/220px-1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_%284637035235%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_%284637035235%29.jpg/330px-1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_%284637035235%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_%284637035235%29.jpg/440px-1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_%284637035235%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1949_Maserati_A6-1500GT_3C_Pinin_Farina_Competition_Berlinetta_-_rvl_(4637035235).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maserati A6 1500 Pinin Farina Competition Berlinetta 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 1950 Coppa Inter-Europa at Monza was held in March. Separate races were held for sports cars, and for <i>Gran Turismo</i> cars in four classes: 750, 1100, 1500 and over 1500.</p>
<p>Ferrari entered, and won, the Sports car 2000 class with a Ferrari 166 MM <i>berlinetta</i>, while an Alfa Romeo <i>Sperimentale</i> (over 2000 class) won the sports car race overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Gran Turismo</i> race was contested by <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Aprilia" title="Lancia Aprilia">Lancia Aprilia</a>, Cisitalia 202B, <a href="/wiki/Automobili_Stanguellini" title="Automobili Stanguellini">Stanguellini GT 1100</a>, Fiat 500, <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_6C" title="Alfa Romeo 6C">Alfa Romeo 2500</a> and Fiat <a href="/wiki/Zagato" title="Zagato">Zagato</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The overall winner was WWII fighter ace <a href="/wiki/Franco_Bordoni" title="Franco Bordoni">Franco Bordoni's</a> <a href="/wiki/Maserati_A6" title="Maserati A6">Maserati A6 1500</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:112_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-:112-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950_Targa_Florio">1950 Targa Florio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1950 Targa Florio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Targa_Florio" title="Targa Florio">Targa Florio</a> in Sicily was held the first weekend of April, and featured a <i>Gran Turismo Internazionale</i> category for the first time, in two classes: 1500 and over 1500. Contested by Lancia Aprilia, Cisitalia 202, Fiat 1100, Maserati A6, and even a solitary British <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Cars" title="Bristol Cars">Bristol</a> (based on the successful pre-war <a href="/wiki/BMW_328" title="BMW 328">BMW 328</a>), the <i>Gran Turismo Internaionzle</i> category was won by Argentinian driver, <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Schwelm_Cruz" title="Adolfo Schwelm Cruz">Adolfo Schwelm Cruz</a>, in an Alfa Romeo 6C 2500 SS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1951_Campionato_Gran_Turismo_Internazionale">1951 Campionato Gran Turismo Internazionale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1951 Campionato Gran Turismo Internazionale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For 1951 the CSAI organised an Italian national championship for the <i>Gran Turismo Internazionale</i> category in four classes: 750, 1500, 2000 and over 2000 cc. Interest was attracted from manufacturers such as Alfa Romeo, <a href="/wiki/Lancia" title="Lancia">Lancia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maserati" title="Maserati">Maserati</a>, Ferrari, Fiat and SIATA. The championship was held over ten events, including all the classic long-distance road races (the Giro di Sicilia, the Mille Miglia, the Coppa della Toscana, the Giro dell'Umbria, the Coppa d' Oro delle Dolomiti, the Giro delle Calabrie and the Stella Alpina) as well as three circuit races (the Coppa Inter-Europa at Monza, the Circuito di Caracalla night race in Rome, and the 6 Ore di Pescara).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Tourer_Characteristics">Grand Tourer Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Grand Tourer Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2165" data-file-width="4489" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg/220px-Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg/330px-Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg/440px-Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jaguar_E-Type_series_1_coup%C3%A9_1964.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Front-engine, rear-wheel drive coupe: 1964 <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_E-Type" title="Jaguar E-Type">Jaguar E-Type</a>. <a href="/wiki/Automotive_design" title="Automotive design">Automotive designers</a> call the position of the driver's hip close to the rear axle "close-coupled".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The terms "grand tourer", "<i>grand turismo</i>", "<i>grand routiere</i>", and "GT" are among the most misused terms in motoring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawson_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-dawson-82">[82]</a></sup> The grand touring designation generally "means motoring at speed, in style, safety, and comfort."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> "Purists define "gran turismo" as the enjoyment, excitement and comfort of open-road touring."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg/220px-Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg/330px-Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg/440px-Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jaguar_XJ-S_rear_seats.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rear seats of a 1982 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaguar_XJ-S" title="Jaguar XJ-S">Jaguar XJ-S</a> HE coupe, showing the 2+2 seating layout.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to one author, "the ideal is of a car with the ability to cross a continent at speed and in comfort yet provide driving thrills when demanded" and it should exhibit the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawson_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-dawson-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The engines "should be able to cope with cruising comfortably at the upper limits on all continental roads without drawbacks or loss of usable power."</li>
<li>"Ideally, the GT car should have been devised by its progenitors as a Grand Tourer, with all associated considerations in mind."</li>
<li>"It should be able to transport at least two in comfort with their luggage and have room to spare — probably in the form of a two plus two (<a href="/wiki/2%2B2_(car_body_style)" title="2+2 (car body style)">2+2</a>) seating arrangement."</li>
<li>The design, both "inside and out, should be geared toward complete control by the driver."</li>
<li>Its "chassis and <a href="/wiki/Suspension_(vehicle)" title="Suspension (vehicle)">suspension</a> provide suitable handling and roadholding on all routes" during travels.</li>
</ul>
<p>Grand tourers emphasize comfort and handling over straight-out high performance or <a href="/wiki/Asceticism" title="Asceticism">ascetic</a>, <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/spartan" title="wikt:spartan">spartan</a> accommodations. In comparison, <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">sports cars</a> (also a "much abused and confused term") are typically more "crude" compared to "sophisticated Grand Touring machinery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> However, the popularity of using GT for marketing purposes has meant that it has become a "much misused term, eventually signifying no more than a slightly tuned version of a family car with trendy wheels and a go-faster stripe on the side."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historically, most GTs have been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Front_mid-engine,_rear-wheel_drive_layout" title="Front mid-engine, rear-wheel drive layout">front-engined with rear-wheel drive</a>, which creates more space for the cabin than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rear_mid-engine,_rear-wheel_drive_layout" title="Rear mid-engine, rear-wheel drive layout">mid-mounted</a> engine layouts. Softer suspensions, greater storage, and more luxurious appointments add to their driving appeal.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="GT_abbreviation_in_marketing"><i>GT</i> abbreviation in marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: GT abbreviation in marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_(1962-64)_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_(2014).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1879" data-file-width="2630" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_%281962-64%29_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_%282014%29.JPG/220px-Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_%281962-64%29_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_%282014%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_%281962-64%29_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_%282014%29.JPG/330px-Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_%281962-64%29_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_%282014%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_%281962-64%29_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_%282014%29.JPG/440px-Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_%281962-64%29_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_%282014%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Cortina_GT_MkI_(1962-64)_arriving_at_Schaffen-Diest_(2014).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1962-64 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Ford Cortina GT</a>: <a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">two-door sedan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1487" data-file-width="2126" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg/220px-Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg/330px-Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg/440px-Volkswagen_Golf_Mk_I_GTI_001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
