1982 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Volkswagen Golf</a> GTI : <a href="/wiki/Hot_hatch" title="Hot hatch">hot hatch</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="740" data-file-width="1280" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg/220px-Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg/330px-Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg/440px-Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Skyline_R34_GT-R_N%C3%BCr_002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1999 <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Skyline_GT-R" title="Nissan Skyline GT-R">Nissan Skyline GT-R</a>: high-performance <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">two-door coupe</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>GT</i> abbreviation is popular across the automotive industry, because of its positive associations with wealth, speed and style. Many vehicles that are not actually <i>gran turismo</i> use this appellation to increase sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-:22-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the many variations of GT are:</p>
<ul>
<li>GT (Gran Turismo) a two-door coupe. For example, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_86" title="Toyota 86">Toyota GT86</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_GT" title="Alfa Romeo GT">Alfa Romeo GT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bentley_Continental_GT" title="Bentley Continental GT">Bentley Continental GT</a>.</li>
<li>GTO (Gran Turismo Omologata) a <a href="/wiki/Homologation_(motorsport)" title="Homologation (motorsport)">homologated</a> car for racing (used by Ferrari, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Motors" title="Mitsubishi Motors">Mitsubishi</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Donkervoort" title="Donkervoort">Donkervoort</a>). Examples include <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_288_GTO" title="Ferrari 288 GTO">Ferrari 288 GTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_250_GTO" title="Ferrari 250 GTO">Ferrari 250 GTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac_GTO" title="Pontiac GTO">Pontiac GTO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_GTO" title="Mitsubishi GTO">Mitsubishi GTO</a>.</li>
<li>GTS (Gran Turismo Spider) a <a href="/wiki/Convertible" title="Convertible">convertible</a> version. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_348" title="Ferrari 348">Ferrari 348 GTS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_308_GTB/GTS" title="Ferrari 308 GTB/GTS">Ferrari 308 GTS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Daytona" title="Ferrari Daytona">Ferrari 365 GTS/4</a>.</li>
<li>GTS (Gran Turismo Sport) a four-door sedan. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_GTS" title="HSV GTS">HSV GTS</a>.</li>
<li>GTS (Grand Tourisme Spécial) used by <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> in their mid-range variants of the "numeric" models, such as <a href="/wiki/Renault_19" title="Renault 19">Renault 19 GTS</a></li>
<li>GTB (Gran Turismo Berlinetta) a coupe style GT. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_328" title="Ferrari 328">Ferrari 328 GTB</a>.</li>
<li>GTV (Gran Turismo Veloce) a "fast" version. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfa-Romeo_GTV" title="Alfa-Romeo GTV">Alfa Romeo GTV6</a>.</li>
<li>GTi (Gran Turismo Iniezione) or <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tourer_Injection" title="Grand Tourer Injection">Grand Tourer Injection</a> - a fuel injected version. First used on the 1961 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maserati_3500" title="Maserati 3500">Maserati 3500</a> GTi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>GTI — <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Volkswagen Golf GTI</a></li>
<li>GT/E or GTE ("Einspritzung" — German for (fuel) "injection") used on the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Manta" title="Opel Manta">Opel Manta</a> GT/E, and Vauxhall performance vehicles, such as the <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Astra#Astra_GTE" title="Vauxhall Astra">Astra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opel_Corsa#Corsa_A_.281982.E2.80.931993.29" title="Opel Corsa">Nova</a> GTE</li>
<li>GTE (Grand Touring Estate) An estate wagon GT. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Reliant_Scimitar" title="Reliant Scimitar">Reliant Scimitar</a> GTE.</li>
<li>GTX (Grand Tourisme Xtreme) used by <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> on their top-of-the-range sports variants of the "numeric" models, example the <a href="/wiki/Renault_21" title="Renault 21">Renault 21 GTX</a></li>
<li>GTA (Gran Turismo Alleggerita /Automatic), for example:
<ul>
<li>(Alleggerita) (lightened) — <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_GTA" title="Alfa Romeo GTA">Alfa Romeo GTA</a></li>
<li>(Automatic) — <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_456" title="Ferrari 456">Ferrari 456 GTA</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Lancer_Evolution_VII" title="Mitsubishi Lancer Evolution VII">Mitsubishi Lancer Evolution VII GT-A</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>GTAm (Gran Turismo Alleggerita Modificata) a modified, lightened model such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_GTAm" title="Alfa Romeo GTAm">Alfa Romeo GTAm</a></li>
<li>GTC can have various meanings, for example:
<ul>
<li>(Gran Turismo Compressore) — <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_6C" title="Alfa Romeo 6C">Alfa Romeo 6C</a> 1750 GTC</li>
<li>(Gran Turismo Cabriolet) — <a href="/wiki/Bentley_Continental_GT" title="Bentley Continental GT">Bentley Continental GT</a>C</li>
<li>(Gran Turismo Compact) — <a href="/wiki/Opel_Astra" title="Opel Astra">Opel Astra</a> GTC</li>
<li>(Gran Turismo Crossover) — <a href="/wiki/Opel_Antara" title="Opel Antara">Opel Antara</a> GTC</li>
<li>(Gran Turismo Corsa) (racing) — an Italian racing version. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferrari_458_Italia#Racing" title="Ferrari 458 Italia">Ferrari 458 Italia GTC</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>GTD (Gran Turismo Diesel), used by Volkswagen in sport-oriented Golf version and Peugeot in lowered Diesel 505 models</li>
<li>GTR or GT-R, (Gran Turismo Racing), as in the <a href="/wiki/McLaren_F1_GTR" title="McLaren F1 GTR">McLaren F1 GTR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_CLK_GTR" title="Mercedes-Benz CLK GTR">Mercedes-Benz CLK GTR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Skyline_GT-R" title="Nissan Skyline GT-R">Nissan Skyline GT-R</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nissan_GT-R" title="Nissan GT-R">Nissan GT-R</a></li>
<li>HGT (High Gran Turismo), used by Fiat for sport-oriented versions of some of its models</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_tourers_in_racing">Grand tourers in racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Grand tourers in racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The term <i>grand tourer,</i> or <i>gran turismo,</i> is sometimes used for race versions of <a href="/wiki/Homologation_(motorsport)" title="Homologation (motorsport)">serial production-based</a> sports cars (even those not fitting the traditional grand tourer definition, but not including non-production <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">prototypes</a>) that take part in <a href="/wiki/Sports_car_racing" title="Sports car racing">sports car racing</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Endurance_racing_(motorsport)" title="Endurance racing (motorsport)">endurance races</a> like the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a>, <a href="/wiki/12_Hours_of_Sebring" title="12 Hours of Sebring">12 Hours of Sebring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petit_Le_Mans" title="Petit Le Mans">Petit Le Mans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mille_Miglia" title="Mille Miglia">Mille Miglia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Targa_Florio" title="Targa Florio">Targa Florio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spa_24_Hours" title="Spa 24 Hours">Spa 24 Hours</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bathurst_12_Hour" title="Bathurst 12 Hour">Bathurst 12 Hour</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carrera_Panamericana" title="Carrera Panamericana">Carrera Panamericana</a>.</p>
<p>Examples of race grand tourers include:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport_classification">Motorsport classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Motorsport classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In some professional motorsport classifications, such as the Grand Touring categories promoted by the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile">FIA</a>, the GT car is defined as an open or closed automobile with no more than one door on each side and at least two seats, one on each side of the longitudinal centre line of the car; these two seats must be crossed by the same transversal plane. This car must be legal to drive on the open road, and adapted for racing on circuits or closed courses.</p>
<p>GT cars are divided, from most powerful to least powerful, into GT1 (formerly GTS and GT) and GT2 (formerly GT and N-GT) in most championships, although the ACO has canceled further GT1 involvement not only in the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> but in every other Le Mans Series (LMS, ALMS, ILMC, JLMC) sanctioned by the ACO. This only left room for GT1 cars to race in the <a href="/wiki/FIA_GT1_World_Championship" title="FIA GT1 World Championship">FIA GT1 World Championship</a>, while in turn GT2 cars only competed in ACO sanctioned event due to the absence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIA_GT2_European_Championship" title="FIA GT2 European Championship">FIA GT2 European Championship</a>. GT3 and GT4 class cars also have their own championships, as well as being eligible for several National GT championships.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples_of_grand_tourers">Examples of grand tourers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Examples of grand tourers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>A true <i>grand tourer</i> is a luxury or performance vehicle intended for long-distance spirited travel in both comfort and style. The placement of "GT" on an automobile does not necessarily classify it as a "grand tourer." Some examples include:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/AC_Frua" title="AC Frua">AC Frua</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_GTV" title="Alfa Romeo GTV">Alfa Romeo GTV</a> (1960s–2005)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_GT" title="Alfa Romeo GT">Alfa Romeo GT</a></li>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peugeot_907" title="Peugeot 907">Peugeot 907 Concept</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_touring_car_tires">Grand touring car tires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_tourer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Grand touring car tires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The term grand touring is used amongst manufacturers of <a href="/wiki/Tire" title="Tire">tires</a> to describe all-season tires that are designed to have higher performance and handling capabilities than a regular passenger car all-season tire with a smoother, more luxurious ride than a performance tire. Most <a href="/wiki/D-segment" title="D-segment">D-segment</a> and larger cars sold in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> come with grand touring tires as original equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tire_Rack_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tire_Rack-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
